      <p>
       <b>
        Honduras
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'h' in 'hi'">
            h
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ʊər/: 'our' in 'tour'">
            ʊər
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Honduras.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/En-us-Honduras.ogg" title="En-us-Honduras.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [onˈduɾas]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Honduras
       </b>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         República de Honduras
        </span>
       </i>
       ), is a
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       . It has at times been referred to as
       <b>
        Spanish Honduras
       </b>
       to differentiate it from
       <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">
        British Honduras
       </a>
       , which became modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Honduras is bordered to the west by
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       , to the southwest by
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       , to the southeast by
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       , to the south by the Pacific Ocean at the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">
        Gulf of Fonseca
       </a>
       , and to the north by the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Honduras" title="Gulf of Honduras">
        Gulf of Honduras
       </a>
       , a large inlet of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Honduras was home to several important
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" title="Mesoamerican">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       cultures, most notably the
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Maya
       </a>
       , before the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish invaded
       </a>
       in the sixteenth century. The Spanish introduced Roman Catholicism and the now predominant
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish language
       </a>
       , along with numerous customs that have blended with the indigenous culture. Honduras became independent in 1821 and has since been a republic, although it has consistently endured much social strife and political instability, and remains one of the poorest countries in the western hemisphere. In 1960, the northern part of what was the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       was transferred from Nicaragua to Honduras by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The nation's economy is primarily agricultural making it especially vulnerable to natural disasters such as Hurricane Mitch in 1998.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:9-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The lower class is primarily agriculturally based while wealth is concentrated in the country's urban centers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Honduras has a Human Development Index of .625, classifying it as a nation with medium development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When the Index is adjusted for income inequality, its Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index is .443.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Honduran society is predominately
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        Mestizo
       </a>
       , however American Indian, Black and White individuals also live in Honduras (2017).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The nation had a relatively high political stability until its 2009 coup and again with the 2017 presidential election.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:7-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Honduras has the world's highest
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate" title="List of countries by intentional homicide rate">
        murder rate
       </a>
       and high levels of sexual violence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Insight_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Insight-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:15_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:15-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Honduras spans about 112,492 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       and has a population exceeding 9 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its northern portions are part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Caribbean_Zone" title="Western Caribbean Zone">
        Western Caribbean Zone
       </a>
       , as reflected in the area's demographics and culture. Honduras is known for its rich natural resources, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minerals" title="Minerals">
        minerals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_fruit" title="Tropical fruit">
        tropical fruit
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">
        sugar cane
       </a>
       , as well as for its growing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Textiles" title="Textiles">
        textiles
       </a>
       industry, which serves the international market.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The literal meaning of the term "Honduras" is "depths" in Spanish. The name could either refer to the bay of Trujillo as an anchorage,
       <i>
        fondura
       </i>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Leonese_dialect" title="Leonese dialect">
        Leonese dialect
       </a>
       of Spanish, or to
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Columbus
       </a>
       's alleged quote that
       <i>
        "Gracias a Dios que hemos salido de esas Honduras"
       </i>
       ("Thank God we have departed from those depths").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davidson2006_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Davidson2006-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It was not until the end of the 16th century that
       <i>
        Honduras
       </i>
       was used for the whole province. Prior to 1580,
       <i>
        Honduras
       </i>
       only referred to the eastern part of the province, and
       <i>
        Higueras
       </i>
       referred to the western part.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davidson2006_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Davidson2006-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another early name is
       <a href="/wiki/Guaimura" title="Guaimura">
        Guaymuras
       </a>
       , revived as the name for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaymuras_dialogue" title="Guaymuras dialogue">
        political dialogue in 2009
       </a>
       that took place in Honduras as opposed to Costa Rica.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoduras_claire_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hoduras_claire-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Hondurans are often referred to as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catracho" title="Catracho">
         Catracho
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Catracha
       </i>
       (fem) in Spanish. The word was coined by
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguans" title="Nicaraguans">
        Nicaraguans
       </a>
       and derives from the last name of the Spanish Honduran General
       <a href="/wiki/Florencio_Xatruch" title="Florencio Xatruch">
        Florencio Xatruch
       </a>
       , who in 1857 led Honduran armed forces against an attempted invasion by North American adventurer
       <a href="/wiki/William_Walker_(filibuster)" title="William Walker (filibuster)">
        William Walker
       </a>
       . The nickname is considered complimentary, not derogatory.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Honduras" title="History of Honduras">
        History of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CPN_ST_B_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="741" data-file-width="1122" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/CPN_ST_B_01.jpg/220px-CPN_ST_B_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/CPN_ST_B_01.jpg/330px-CPN_ST_B_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/CPN_ST_B_01.jpg/440px-CPN_ST_B_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CPN_ST_B_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Maya_stelae" title="Maya stelae">
          Maya stela
         </a>
         , an emblematic symbol of the Honduran Mayan civilization at Copan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">
        Pre-colonial period
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_chronology" title="Mesoamerican chronology">
        Mesoamerican chronology
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Bajo_Agu%C3%A1n" title="Bajo Aguán">
        Bajo Aguán
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In pre-Columbian times, modern Honduras was part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       cultural area. In the west, Mayan civilization flourished for hundreds of years. The dominant state within Honduras' borders was in
       <a href="/wiki/Cop%C3%A1n" title="Copán">
        Copán
       </a>
       . Copán fell with the other Lowland centres during the conflagrations of the
       <a href="/wiki/Classic_Maya_collapse" title="Classic Maya collapse">
        Terminal Classic
       </a>
       in the 9th century. The Maya of this civilization survive in western Honduras as the
       <a href="/wiki/Ch%27orti%27_people" title="Ch'orti' people">
        Ch'orti'
       </a>
       , isolated from their Choltian linguistic peers to the west.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Remnants of other Pre-Columbian cultures are found throughout the country. Archaeologists have studied sites such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Naco_(Honduras)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Naco (Honduras) (page does not exist)">
        Naco
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naco_(Honduras)" title="es:Naco (Honduras)">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       and La Sierra in the Naco Valley,
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Naranjos,_Honduras" title="Los Naranjos, Honduras">
        Los Naranjos
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Yojoa" title="Lake Yojoa">
        Lake Yojoa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yarumela" title="Yarumela">
        Yarumela
       </a>
       in the Comayagua Valley,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/La_Ceiba" title="La Ceiba">
        La Ceiba
       </a>
       and Salitron Viejo
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (both now under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Cajon_Dam_(Honduras)" title="El Cajon Dam (Honduras)">
        Cajon Dam
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">
        reservoir
       </a>
       ), Selin Farm and Cuyamel in the Aguan valley,
       <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Palenque" title="Cerro Palenque">
        Cerro Palenque
       </a>
       , Travesia, Curruste, Ticamaya, Despoloncal in the lower Ulua river valley, and many others.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish_conquest_.281524.E2.80.931539.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_conquest_(1524–1539)">
        Spanish conquest (1524–1539)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Honduras" title="Spanish conquest of Honduras">
        Spanish conquest of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1109" data-file-width="880" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg/199px-Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg/299px-Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg/398px-Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg 2x" width="199"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cortes-Hernan-LOC.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hernán Cortés, one of the conquerors of Honduras.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On his fourth and the final voyage to the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       in 1502,
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       landed near the modern town of
       <a href="/wiki/Trujillo,_Honduras" title="Trujillo, Honduras">
        Trujillo
       </a>
       , near Guaimoreto Lagoon, becaming the first European to visit the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">
        Bay Islands
       </a>
       on the coast of Honduras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 30 July 1502 Columbus sent his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Columbus" title="Bartholomew Columbus">
        Bartholomew
       </a>
       to explore the islands and Bartholomew encountered a Mayan trading vessel from Yucatán, carrying well-dressed Maya and a rich cargo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerramon1986242Clendinnen20033–4_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerramon1986242Clendinnen20033–4-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bartholomew's men stole the cargo they wanted and kidnapped the ship's elderly captain to serve as an interpreter
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClendinnen20033–4_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClendinnen20033–4-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the first recorded encounter between the Spanish and the Maya.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharerTraxler2006758_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharerTraxler2006758-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 1524,
       <a href="/wiki/Gil_Gonz%C3%A1lez_D%C3%A1vila" title="Gil González Dávila">
        Gil González Dávila
       </a>
       became the first Spaniard to enter Honduras as a
       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">
        conquistador
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apuntes_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Apuntes-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guide_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guide-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">
        Hernán Cortés
       </a>
       , who had brought forces down from Mexico. Much of the conquest took place in the following two decades, first by groups loyal to
       <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Olid" title="Cristóbal de Olid">
        Cristóbal de Olid
       </a>
       , and then by those loyal to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Montejo" title="Francisco Montejo">
        Francisco Montejo
       </a>
       but most particularly by those following Alvarado
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2017)">
           who?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . In addition to Spanish resources, the conquerors relied heavily on armed forces from Mexico—
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tlaxcalans" title="Tlaxcalans">
        Tlaxcalans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Mexica
       </a>
       armies of thousands who remained garrisoned in the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Resistance to conquest was led in particular by
       <a href="/wiki/Lempira_(Lenca_ruler)" title="Lempira (Lenca ruler)">
        Lempira
       </a>
       . Many regions in the north of Honduras never fell to the Spanish, notably the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Miskito Kingdom
       </a>
       . After the Spanish conquest, Honduras became part of Spain's vast empire in the New World within the
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">
        Kingdom of Guatemala
       </a>
       . Trujillo and
       <a href="/wiki/Gracias_a_Dios_Department" title="Gracias a Dios Department">
        Gracias
       </a>
       were the first city-capitals. The Spanish ruled the region for approximately three centuries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish_Honduras_.281524.E2.80.931821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Honduras_(1524–1821)">
        Spanish Honduras (1524–1821)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Honduras was organized as a province of the
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">
        Kingdom of Guatemala
       </a>
       and the capital was fixed, first at Trujillo on the Atlantic coast, and later at
       <a href="/wiki/Comayagua" title="Comayagua">
        Comayagua
       </a>
       , and finally at
       <a href="/wiki/Tegucigalpa" title="Tegucigalpa">
        Tegucigalpa
       </a>
       in the central part of the country.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Silver_mining" title="Silver mining">
        Silver mining
       </a>
       was a key factor in the Spanish conquest and settlement of Honduras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson1_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson1-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Initially the mines were worked by local people through the
       <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">
        encomienda
       </a>
       system, but as disease and resistance made this option less available, slaves from other parts of Central America were brought in. When local slave trading stopped at the end of the sixteenth century, African slaves, mostly from
       <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">
        Angola
       </a>
       , were imported.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cost_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cost-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After about 1650, very few slaves or other outside workers arrived in Honduras.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the Spanish conquered the southern or Pacific portion of Honduras fairly quickly, they were less successful on the northern, or Atlantic side. They managed to found a few towns along the coast, at
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Puerto Cortés">
        Puerto Caballos
       </a>
       and Trujillo in particular, but failed to conquer the eastern portion of the region and many pockets of independent indigenous people as well. The
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Miskito Kingdom
       </a>
       in the northeast was particularly effective at resisting conquest. The Miskito Kingdom found support from northern European privateers, pirates and especially the British formerly English colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Jamaica
       </a>
       , which placed much of the area under its protection after 1740.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg/300px-Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg/450px-Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg/600px-Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Exterior_Fuerte_de_Omoa_Honduras.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Fernando_de_Omoa" title="Battle of San Fernando de Omoa">
          Fortaleza de San Fernando de Omoa
         </a>
         was built by the Spanish to protect the coast of Honduras from English pirates.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1821)">
        Independence (1821)
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Honduras gained independence from Spain in 1821 and was a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">
        First Mexican Empire
       </a>
       until 1823, when it became part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_Central_America" title="United Provinces of Central America">
        United Provinces of Central America
       </a>
       . It has been an independent republic and has held regular elections since 1838. In the 1840s and 1850s Honduras participated in several failed attempts at Central American unity, such as the Confederation of Central America (1842–1845), the covenant of Guatemala (1842), the Diet of Sonsonate (1846), the Diet of Nacaome (1847) and National Representation in Central America (1849–1852). Although Honduras eventually adopted the name Republic of Honduras, the unionist ideal never waned, and Honduras was one of the Central American countries that pushed the hardest for a policy of regional unity.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">
        Neoliberal
       </a>
       policies favoring
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        international trade
       </a>
       and investment began in the 1870s, and soon foreign interests became involved, first in shipping from the north coast, especially tropical fruit and most notably bananas, and then in building railroads. In 1888, a projected railroad line from the Caribbean coast to the capital,
       <a href="/wiki/Tegucigalpa" title="Tegucigalpa">
        Tegucigalpa
       </a>
       , ran out of money when it reached
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pedro_Sula" title="San Pedro Sula">
        San Pedro Sula
       </a>
       . As a result, San Pedro grew into the nation's primary industrial center and second-largest city.
       <a href="/wiki/Comayagua" title="Comayagua">
        Comayagua
       </a>
       was the capital of Honduras until 1880, when the capital moved to Tegucigalpa.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since independence, nearly 300 small internal rebellions and civil wars have occurred in the country, including some changes of régime.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">
        20th century
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the late nineteenth century, Honduras granted land and substantial exemptions to several US-based fruit and infrastructure companies in return for developing the country's northern regions. Thousands of workers came to the north coast as a result to work in
       <a href="/wiki/Banana_production_in_Honduras" title="Banana production in Honduras">
        banana plantations
       </a>
       and other businesses that grew up around the export industry. Banana-exporting companies, dominated until 1930 by the
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyamel_Fruit_Company" title="Cuyamel Fruit Company">
        Cuyamel Fruit Company
       </a>
       , as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Fruit_Company" title="United Fruit Company">
        United Fruit Company
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Fruit_Company" title="Standard Fruit Company">
        Standard Fruit Company
       </a>
       , built an
       <a href="/wiki/Enclave_economy" title="Enclave economy">
        enclave economy
       </a>
       in northern Honduras, controlling
       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">
        infrastructure
       </a>
       and creating self-sufficient, tax-exempt sectors that contributed relatively little to economic growth. American troops landed in Honduras in 1903, 1907, 1911, 1912, 1919, 1924 and 1925.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becker_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Becker-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1904 the writer
       <a href="/wiki/O._Henry" title="O. Henry">
        O. Henry
       </a>
       coined the term "
       <a href="/wiki/Banana_republic" title="Banana republic">
        banana republic
       </a>
       " to describe Honduras,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       publishing a book called
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabbages_and_Kings_(literature)" title="Cabbages and Kings (literature)">
         Cabbages and Kings
        </a>
       </i>
       , about a fictional country, Anchuria, inspired by his experiences in Honduras, where he had lived for six months.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <i>
        The Admiral
       </i>
       , O.Henry refers to the nation as a "small maritime banana republic"; naturally, the fruit was the entire basis of its economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to a literary analyst writing for
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">
         The Economist
        </a>
       </i>
       , "his phrase neatly conjures up the image of a tropical, agrarian country. But its real meaning is sharper: it refers to the fruit companies from the United States that came to exert extraordinary influence over the politics of Honduras and its neighbors."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition to drawing Central American workers north, the fruit companies encouraged immigration of workers from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-speaking_Caribbean" title="English-speaking Caribbean">
        English-speaking Caribbean
       </a>
       , notably
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Jamaica
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       , which introduced an African-descended, English-speaking and largely Protestant population into the country, although many of these workers left following changes to immigration law in 1939.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chambers_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chambers-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Honduras joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Allied Nations
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">
        Pearl Harbor
       </a>
       , on 8 December 1941, and signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">
        Declaration by United Nations
       </a>
       on 1 January 1942 along with twenty-five other governments.
      </p>
      <p>
       Constitutional crises in the 1940s led to reforms in the 1950s. One reform gave workers permission to organize, and a 1954
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_strike_of_1954_(Honduras)" title="General strike of 1954 (Honduras)">
        general strike
       </a>
       paralyzed the northern part of the country for more than two months, but led to reforms. In 1963 a
       <a href="/wiki/1963_Honduran_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1963 Honduran coup d'état">
        military coup
       </a>
       unseated democratically elected President
       <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Villeda_Morales" title="Ramón Villeda Morales">
        Ramón Villeda Morales
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1960, the northern part of what was the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       was transferred from Nicaragua to Honduras by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1969 Honduras and
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       fought what became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">
        Football War
       </a>
       . Border tensions led to acrimony between the two countries after
       <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_L%C3%B3pez_Arellano" title="Oswaldo López Arellano">
        Oswaldo López Arellano
       </a>
       , the president of Honduras, blamed the deteriorating Honduran economy on immigrants from El Salvador. The relationship reached a low when El Salvador met Honduras for a three-round football elimination match preliminary to the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        World Cup
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FW_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FW-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tensions escalated and on 14 July 1969, the Salvadoran army launched an attack on the Honduran army
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)">
          <span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2016)">
           where?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       negotiated a cease-fire which took effect on 20 July and brought about a withdrawal of Salvadoran troops in early August.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FW_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FW-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Contributing factors to the conflict were a boundary dispute and the presence of thousands of Salvadorans living in Honduras illegally. After the week-long war as many as 130,000 Salvadoran immigrants were expelled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fifi" title="Hurricane Fifi">
        Hurricane Fifi
       </a>
       caused severe damage when it skimmed the northern coast of Honduras on 18 and 19 September 1974.
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Alberto_Melgar_Castro" title="Juan Alberto Melgar Castro">
        Melgar Castro
       </a>
       (1975–78) and Paz Garcia (1978–82) largely built the current physical infrastructure and telecommunications system of Honduras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOS-Honduras_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-DOS-Honduras-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="611" data-file-width="814" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG/300px-Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG/450px-Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG/600px-Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitch-Tegucigalpa_Damage.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Part of the massive damage caused by
         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">
          Hurricane Mitch
         </a>
         in Tegucigalpa, 1998
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1979, the country returned to civilian rule . A
       <a href="/wiki/Constituent_assembly" title="Constituent assembly">
        constituent assembly
       </a>
       was popularly elected in April 1980 to write a new constitution, and general elections were held in November 1981. The constitution was approved in 1982 and the
       <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Honduras" title="Liberal Party of Honduras">
        PLH
       </a>
       government of
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Suazo_C%C3%B3rdova" title="Roberto Suazo Córdova">
        Roberto Suazo
       </a>
       won the election with a promise to carry out an ambitious program of economic and social development to tackle the recession Honduras was in. He launched ambitious social and economic development projects sponsored by American development aid. Honduras became host to the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">
        Peace Corps
       </a>
       mission in the world, and nongovernmental and international voluntary agencies proliferated. The Peace Corps withdrew its volunteers in 2012, citing safety concerns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSM_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CSM-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the early 1980s the United States established a continuing military presence in Honduras to support El Salvador, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contra_(guerrillas)" title="Contra (guerrillas)">
        Contra
       </a>
       guerrillas fighting the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaraguan
       </a>
       government, and also develop an air strip and modern port in Honduras. Though spared the bloody civil wars wracking its neighbors, the Honduran army quietly waged campaigns against
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" title="Marxist-Leninist">
        Marxist-Leninist
       </a>
       militias such as the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Movement-Chinchoneros" title="People's Liberation Movement-Chinchoneros">
        Cinchoneros
       </a>
       Popular Liberation Movement, notorious for kidnappings and bombings,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and against many non-militants as well. The operation included a CIA-backed campaign of extrajudicial killings by government-backed units, most notably
       <a href="/wiki/Battalion_3-16_(Honduras)" title="Battalion 3-16 (Honduras)">
        Battalion 316
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1998,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">
        Hurricane Mitch
       </a>
       caused massive and widespread destruction. Honduran President
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Roberto_Flores" title="Carlos Roberto Flores">
        Carlos Roberto Flores
       </a>
       said that fifty years of progress in the country had been reversed. Mitch destroyed about 70% of the country's crops and an estimated 70–80% of the transportation infrastructure, including nearly all bridges and secondary roads. Across Honduras 33,000 houses were destroyed, and an additional 50,000 damaged. Some 5,000 people killed, and 12,000 more injured. Total losses were estimated at $3 billion USD.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">
        21st century
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="300" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg/199px-Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg/299px-Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg 2x" width="199"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Honduras.RicardoMaduro.01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ricardo Maduro
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Zelaya_detail,_ABR_August_07,_2007_cortado.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="273" data-file-width="303" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Manuel_Zelaya_detail%2C_ABR_August_07%2C_2007_cortado.jpg/199px-Manuel_Zelaya_detail%2C_ABR_August_07%2C_2007_cortado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Manuel_Zelaya_detail%2C_ABR_August_07%2C_2007_cortado.jpg/299px-Manuel_Zelaya_detail%2C_ABR_August_07%2C_2007_cortado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/73/Manuel_Zelaya_detail%2C_ABR_August_07%2C_2007_cortado.jpg 2x" width="199"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manuel_Zelaya_detail,_ABR_August_07,_2007_cortado.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Manuel Zelaya
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 2008 Honduran floods were severe and damaged or destroyed around half of the roads as a result.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Honduran_political_crisis" title="2009 Honduran political crisis">
        constitutional crisis
       </a>
       resulted when power transferred in a coup from the president to the head of Congress. The
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       (OAS) suspended Honduras because it did not feel its government was legitimate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OAS_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OAS-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Honduran_leader_sworn_in_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Honduran_leader_sworn_in-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Countries around the world, the OAS, and the United Nations
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       formally and unanimously condemned the action as a
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       , refusing to recognize the
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       government, even though the lawyers consulted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
        Library of Congress
       </a>
       submitted to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
        United States Congress
       </a>
       an opinion that declared the coup legal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honduran_Supreme_Court" title="Honduran Supreme Court">
        Honduran Supreme Court
       </a>
       also ruled that the proceedings had been legal. The government that followed the
       <i>
        de facto government
       </i>
       established a truth and reconciliation commission,
       <i>
        Comisión de la Verdad y Reconciliación
       </i>
       , which after more than a year of research and debate concluded that the ousting had been a
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       , and illegal in the commission's opinion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Honduras" title="Geography of Honduras">
        Geography of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Un-honduras.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2433" data-file-width="3277" height="483" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Un-honduras.png/650px-Un-honduras.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Un-honduras.png/975px-Un-honduras.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Un-honduras.png/1300px-Un-honduras.png 2x" width="650"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Un-honduras.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of Honduras.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The north coast of Honduras borders the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       and the Pacific Ocean lies south through the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">
        Gulf of Fonseca
       </a>
       . Honduras consists mainly of mountains, with narrow plains along the coasts. A large undeveloped lowland jungle,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Mosquitia" title="La Mosquitia">
         La Mosquitia
        </a>
       </i>
       lies in the northeast, and the heavily populated lowland Sula valley in the northwest. In La Mosquitia lies the
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       world-heritage site
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Pl%C3%A1tano_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Río Plátano Biosphere Reserve">
        Río Plátano Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       , with the
       <a href="/wiki/Coco_River" title="Coco River">
        Coco River
       </a>
       which divides Honduras from
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islas_de_la_Bah%C3%ADa" title="Islas de la Bahía">
        Islas de la Bahía
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Swan_Islands,_Honduras" title="Swan Islands, Honduras">
        Swan Islands
       </a>
       are off the north coast.
       <a href="/wiki/Misteriosa_Bank" title="Misteriosa Bank">
        Misteriosa Bank
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Bank" title="Rosario Bank">
        Rosario Bank
       </a>
       , 130 to 130 to 150 kilometres (81 to 93 miles) north of the Swan Islands, fall within the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">
        Exclusive Economic Zone
       </a>
       (EEZ) of Honduras.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg/300px-MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg/450px-MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg/600px-MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MontanasdelaSierradeAgalta_Honduras.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Honduran rainforest.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Natural resources include timber, gold, silver, copper, lead,
       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">
        zinc
       </a>
       , iron ore,
       <a href="/wiki/Antimony" title="Antimony">
        antimony
       </a>
       , coal, fish, shrimp, and
       <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">
        hydropower
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Honduras_koppen.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="711" data-file-width="765" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Honduras_koppen.svg/250px-Honduras_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Honduras_koppen.svg/375px-Honduras_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Honduras_koppen.svg/500px-Honduras_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Honduras_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_system" title="Köppen climate classification system">
          Köppen climate types
         </a>
         of Honduras
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The climate varies from tropical in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lowland" title="Lowland">
        lowlands
       </a>
       to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">
        temperate
       </a>
       in the mountains. The central and southern regions are relatively hotter and less humid than the northern coast.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Honduras" title="List of birds of Honduras">
        List of birds of Honduras
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Baja_Agu%C3%A1n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Baja Aguán (page does not exist)">
        Baja Aguán
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The region is considered a
       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">
        biodiversity hotspot
       </a>
       because of the many plant and animal species found there. Like other countries in the region, it contains vast biological resources. Honduras hosts more than 6,000 species of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" title="Vascular plants">
        vascular plants
       </a>
       , of which 630 (described so far) are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">
        orchids
       </a>
       ; around 250
       <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">
        reptiles
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">
        amphibians
       </a>
       , more than 700 bird species, and 110
       <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">
        mammalian
       </a>
       species, of which half are
       <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">
        bats
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the northeastern region of
       <a href="/wiki/La_Mosquitia" title="La Mosquitia">
        La Mosquitia
       </a>
       lies the
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Pl%C3%A1tano_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Río Plátano Biosphere Reserve">
        Río Plátano Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       , a lowland rainforest which is home to a great diversity of life. The reserve was added to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage" title="UNESCO World Heritage">
        UNESCO World Heritage
       </a>
       Sites List in 1982.
      </p>
      <p>
       Honduras has rain forests,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cloud_forests" title="Cloud forests">
        cloud forests
       </a>
       (which can rise up to nearly three thousand metres or 9,800 feet
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangroves" title="Mangroves">
        mangroves
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savannas" title="Savannas">
        savannas
       </a>
       and mountain ranges with pine and oak trees, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_Barrier_Reef_System" title="Mesoamerican Barrier Reef System">
        Mesoamerican Barrier Reef System
       </a>
       . In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_(department)" title="Bay Islands (department)">
        Bay Islands
       </a>
       there are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphins" title="Bottlenose dolphins">
        bottlenose dolphins
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manta_rays" title="Manta rays">
        manta rays
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parrot_fish" title="Parrot fish">
        parrot fish
       </a>
       , schools of
       <a href="/wiki/Acanthurus_coeruleus" title="Acanthurus coeruleus">
        blue tang
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">
        whale shark
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">
        Environmental issues
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        Deforestation
       </a>
       resulting from
       <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">
        logging
       </a>
       is rampant in
       <a href="/wiki/Olancho_Department" title="Olancho Department">
        Olancho Department
       </a>
       . The clearing of land for agriculture is prevalent in the largely undeveloped
       <a href="/wiki/La_Mosquitia" title="La Mosquitia">
        La Mosquitia
       </a>
       region, causing land degradation and soil erosion.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Yojoa" title="Lake Yojoa">
        Lake Yojoa
       </a>
       , which is Honduras' largest source of fresh water, is polluted by
       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">
        heavy metals
       </a>
       produced from
       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">
        mining
       </a>
       activities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some rivers and streams are also polluted by mining.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Honduras" title="Politics of Honduras">
        Politics of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honduras is governed within a framework of a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Honduras" title="President of Honduras">
        President of Honduras
       </a>
       is both
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Honduras" title="Government of Honduras">
        Honduran government
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        Legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Honduras" title="National Congress of Honduras">
        National Congress of Honduras
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judiciary
       </a>
       is independent of both the executive branch and the legislature.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Honduras" title="National Congress of Honduras">
        National Congress of Honduras
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Congreso Nacional
       </i>
       ) has 128 members (
       <i>
        diputados
       </i>
       ), elected for a four-year term by
       <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">
        proportional representation
       </a>
       . Congressional seats are assigned the parties' candidates on a
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Honduras" title="Departments of Honduras">
        departmental basis
       </a>
       in proportion to the number of votes each party receives.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">
        Political culture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="570" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg/200px-Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg/300px-Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg/400px-Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presidente_Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Incumbent President
         <a href="/wiki/Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Juan Orlando Hernández">
          Juan Orlando Hernández
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1963, a military coup removed the democratically elected president,
       <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Villeda_Morales" title="Ramón Villeda Morales">
        Ramón Villeda Morales
       </a>
       . A string of authoritarian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">
        military governments
       </a>
       held power uninterrupted until 1981, when
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Suazo_C%C3%B3rdova" title="Roberto Suazo Córdova">
        Roberto Suazo Córdova
       </a>
       was elected president.
      </p>
      <p>
       The party system was dominated by the conservative
       <a href="/wiki/National_Party_of_Honduras" title="National Party of Honduras">
        National Party of Honduras
       </a>
       (Partido Nacional de Honduras: PNH) and the liberal
       <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Honduras" title="Liberal Party of Honduras">
        Liberal Party of Honduras
       </a>
       (Partido Liberal de Honduras: PLH) until the
       <a href="/wiki/2009_Honduran_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2009 Honduran coup d'état">
        2009 Honduran coup d'état
       </a>
       removed
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Zelaya" title="Manuel Zelaya">
        Manuel Zelaya
       </a>
       from office and put
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Micheletti" title="Roberto Micheletti">
        Roberto Micheletti
       </a>
       in his place.
      </p>
      <p>
       Current Honduran president
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Juan Orlando Hernández">
        Juan Orlando Hernández
       </a>
       took office on 27 January 2014. After managing to stand for a second term,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a very close election in 2017 left uncertainty as to whether Hernandez or his main challenger, television personality
       <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Nasralla" title="Salvador Nasralla">
        Salvador Nasralla
       </a>
       , had prevailed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AP-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Panama_Papers">
        Panama Papers
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Two Honduran names that surfaced in the
       <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">
        Panama Papers
       </a>
       disclosures belong to highly successful businessmen from some of Honduras' most prominent families. Jaime Rosenthal and Gilberto Goldstein are among the elite of Honduras, both successful businessmen and politicians. Rosenthal was a
       <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Honduras" title="Vice President of Honduras">
        vice-president
       </a>
       in the 1980s administration of
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Azcona_del_Hoyo" title="José Azcona del Hoyo">
        José Azcona del Hoyo
       </a>
       . His son César Rosenthal was, according to the Panama Papers, the sole stockholder of Renton Management S.A., a Panamanian entity created to purchase airplanes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Honduras" title="Foreign relations of Honduras">
        Foreign relations of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honduras and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       had tense relations throughout 2000 and early 2001 due to a boundary dispute off the Atlantic coast. Nicaragua imposed a 35%
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariff
       </a>
       against Honduran goods due to the dispute.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2009 a
       <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
        coup d'état
       </a>
       ousted President
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Zelaya" title="Manuel Zelaya">
        Manuel Zelaya
       </a>
       ; he was taken in a military aircraft to neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       . The General Assembly of the United Nations voted to denounce the coup and called for the restoration of Zelaya. Several
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin American
       </a>
       nations including Mexico temporarily severed diplomatic relations with Honduras. In July 2010, full diplomatic relations were once again re-established with Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United States sent out mixed messages after the coup; Obama called the ouster a coup and expressed support for Zelaya's return to power. US Secretary of State
       <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">
        Hillary Clinton
       </a>
       , advised by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Negroponte" title="John Negroponte">
        John Negroponte
       </a>
       , the former Reagan-era to Honduras implicated in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran-Contra" title="Iran-Contra">
        Iran-Contra
       </a>
       affair, refrained from expressing support.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She has since explained that the US would have had to cut aid if it called Zelaya's ouster a military coup, although the US has a record of ignoring these events when it chooses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Zelaya had expressed an interest in Hugo Chávez'
       <a href="/wiki/ALBA" title="ALBA">
        Bolivarian Alliance for Peoples of our America
       </a>
       (ALBA), and had actually joined in 2008. After the 2009 coup, Honduras withdrew its membership.
      </p>
      <p>
       This interest in regional agreements may have increased the alarm of establishment politicians. When Zelaya began calling for a "fourth ballot box" to determine whether Hondurans wished to convoke a special constitutional congress, this sounded a lot to some like the constitutional amendments that had extended the terms of both
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugo_Chavez" title="Hugo Chavez">
        Hugo Chavez
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
        Evo Morales
       </a>
       . "Chavez has served as a role model for like-minded leaders intent on cementing their power. These presidents are barely in office when they typically convene a constitutional convention to guarantee their reelection," said a 2009 Spiegel International analysis,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spiegel_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-spiegel-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which noted that one reason to join ALBA was discounted Venezuelan oil. In addition to Chavez and Morales,
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Menem" title="Carlos Menem">
        Carlos Menem
       </a>
       of Argentina,
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Henrique_Cardoso" title="Fernando Henrique Cardoso">
        Fernando Henrique Cardoso
       </a>
       of Brazil and Columbian President
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Uribe" title="Álvaro Uribe">
        Álvaro Uribe
       </a>
       had all taken this step, and Washington and the EU were both accusing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandanista" title="Sandanista">
        Sandanista
       </a>
       government in Nicaragua of tampering with election results.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spiegel_62-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-spiegel-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Politicians of all stripes expressed opposition to Zelaya's referendum proposal, and the Attorney-General accused him of violating the constitution. The Honduran Supreme Court agreed, saying that the constitution had put the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Electoral_Tribunal_(Honduras)" title="Supreme Electoral Tribunal (Honduras)">
        Supreme Electoral Tribunal
       </a>
       in charge of elections and referenda, not the National Statistics Institute, which Zelaya had proposed to have run the count.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crs_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-crs-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Whether or not Zelaya's removal from power had constitutional elements, the Honduran constitution explicitly protects all Hondurans from forced expulsion for Honduras.
      </p>
      <p>
       The United States maintains a small military presence at one Honduran base. The two countries conduct joint peacekeeping, counter-narcotics, humanitarian, disaster relief, humanitarian, medical and civic action exercises. U.S. troops conduct and provide logistics support for a variety of bilateral and multilateral exercises. The United States is Honduras' chief trading partner.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOS-Honduras_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-DOS-Honduras-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Honduras" title="Military of Honduras">
        Military of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honduras has a military with the Honduran Army, Honduran Navy and
       <a href="/wiki/Honduran_Air_Force" title="Honduran Air Force">
        Honduran Air Force
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Honduras" title="Departments of Honduras">
        Departments of Honduras
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Honduras" title="Municipalities of Honduras">
        Municipalities of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HondurasDivisions.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="242" data-file-width="400" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/HondurasDivisions.png/350px-HondurasDivisions.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/HondurasDivisions.png 1.5x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HondurasDivisions.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The departmental divisions of Honduras.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Honduras is divided into 18
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Honduras" title="Departments of Honduras">
        departments
       </a>
       . The capital city is Tegucigalpa in the Central District within the department of
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Moraz%C3%A1n" title="Francisco Morazán">
        Francisco Morazán
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <p>
       A new administrative division called
       <a href="/wiki/Zone_for_Employment_and_Economic_Development_(Honduras)" title="Zone for Employment and Economic Development (Honduras)">
        ZEDE
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Zonas de empleo y desarrollo económico
       </i>
       ) was created in 2013. ZEDEs have a high level of autonomy with their own political system at a judicial, economic and administrative level, and are based on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_market_capitalism" title="Free market capitalism">
        free market capitalism
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Honduras" title="Economy of Honduras">
        Economy of Honduras
       </a>
      </div>
